     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        Game of Thrones
       </b>
      </i>
      is an American
      <a href="/wiki/Fantasy" title="Fantasy">
       fantasy
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_drama" title="Television drama">
       drama
      </a>
      television series created for
      <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">
       HBO
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Showrunner" title="Showrunner">
       showrunners
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Benioff" title="David Benioff">
       David Benioff
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/D._B._Weiss" title="D. B. Weiss">
       D. B. Weiss
      </a>
      . It is an adaptation of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">
        A Song of Ice and Fire
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/George_R._R._Martin" title="George R. R. Martin">
       George R. R. Martin
      </a>
      's series of fantasy novels, the first of which is titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Game_of_Thrones" title="A Game of Thrones">
        A Game of Thrones
       </a>
      </i>
      . Filmed in a
      <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">
       Belfast
      </a>
      studio and on location elsewhere in
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">
       Northern Ireland
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
       Croatia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">
       Iceland
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
       Malta
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
       Scotland
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      , it premiered on HBO in the United States on April 17, 2011. The series completed airing its fifth season on June 14, 2015, and has been renewed for a sixth season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Season_5_.26_6_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Season_5_.26_6-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The series, set on the fictional continents of
      <a href="/wiki/World_of_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="World of A Song of Ice and Fire">
       Westeros and Essos
      </a>
      at the end of a decade-long summer, interweaves several plot lines with a broad
      <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">
       ensemble cast
      </a>
      . The first narrative arc follows a civil war among several noble houses for the
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Throne_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Iron Throne (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Iron Throne
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seven_Kingdoms_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Seven Kingdoms (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Seven Kingdoms
      </a>
      ; the second covers the attempts of the exiled last
      <a href="/wiki/Lineal_descendant" title="Lineal descendant">
       scion
      </a>
      of the realm's deposed ruling dynasty to reclaim the throne; the third chronicles the rising threat of the impending winter and the legendary creatures and fierce peoples of the North.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has attracted record numbers of viewers on HBO and obtained an exceptionally broad and active international
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fan_base" title="Fan base">
       fan base
      </a>
      . It received widespread acclaim by critics, although its frequent use of nudity, violence and sexual violence has attracted criticism. The series has won numerous awards and nominations, including a
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Drama Series">
       Primetime Emmy Award nomination for Outstanding Drama Series
      </a>
      for its first four seasons, a
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Television_Series_%E2%80%93_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Television Series  Drama">
       Golden Globe Award nomination for Best Television Series  Drama
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation" title="Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation">
       Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation
      </a>
      in both Long Form and Short Form, and a
      <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">
       Peabody Award
      </a>
      . Among the ensemble cast,
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">
       Peter Dinklage
      </a>
      has won an
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actor_in_a_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actor in a Drama Series">
       Emmy
      </a>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor_%E2%80%93_Series,_Miniseries_or_Television_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actor  Series, Miniseries or Television Film">
       Golden Globe
      </a>
      for his performance as
      <a href="/wiki/Tyrion_Lannister" title="Tyrion Lannister">
       Tyrion Lannister
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">
       Plot
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Game_of_Thrones_episodes" title="List of Game of Thrones episodes">
       List of Game of Thrones episodes
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire#Plot_synopsis" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">
       Synopsis of A Song of Ice and Fire
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2457" data-file-width="3110" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg/220px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg/330px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg/440px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Weapons.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Power and violence are central themes of
        <i>
         Game of Thrones
        </i>
        , and the great number of weapons made for the series  some of which are shown in this exhibit  reflects this.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      roughly follows the storylines set out in
      <i>
       A Song of Ice and Fire
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Set in the fictional Seven Kingdoms of Westeros, the series chronicles the violent dynastic struggles among the realm's noble families for control of the Iron Throne. As the series opens, additional threats emerge in the icy North and in the eastern continent of Essos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gotfactsheet_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gotfactsheet-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first season is a faithful adaptation of the novel. Later seasons, however, began to diverge with significant changes. According to David Benioff, the show is "about adapting the series as a whole and following the map George laid out for us and hitting the major milestones, but not necessarily each of the stops along the way."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The novels and their adaptation derive aspects of their settings, characters and plot from various events of European history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A principal inspiration for the novels is the English
      <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">
       Wars of the Roses
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (145585) between the houses of
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">
       Lancaster
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">
       York
      </a>
      , reflected in Martin's houses of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lannister" title="Lannister">
       Lannister
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Characters_in_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire#House_Stark" title="Characters in A Song of Ice and Fire">
       Stark
      </a>
      . Most of Westeros, with its castles and knightly tournaments, is reminiscent of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Medieval" title="High Medieval">
       High Medieval
      </a>
      Western Europe. The scheming Cersei, for instance, calls to mind
      <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_France" title="Isabella of France">
       Isabella
      </a>
      , the "she-wolf of France" (12951358).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She and her family, as depicted in
      <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Druon" title="Maurice Druon">
       Maurice Druon
      </a>
      's historical novel series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Accursed_Kings" title="The Accursed Kings">
        The Accursed Kings
       </a>
      </i>
      , in particular, inspired Martin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other historical inspirations for elements of the series include
      <a href="/wiki/Hadrian%27s_Wall" title="Hadrian's Wall">
       Hadrian's Wall
      </a>
      (which became Martin's great Wall), the legend of
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantis" title="Atlantis">
       Atlantis
      </a>
      (ancient
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valyria" title="Valyria">
       Valyria
      </a>
      ), Byzantine "
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_fire" title="Greek fire">
       Greek fire
      </a>
      " ("wildfire"), Icelandic
      <a href="/wiki/Saga" title="Saga">
       sagas
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">
       Viking Age
      </a>
      (the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ironborn" title="Ironborn">
       Ironborn
      </a>
      ) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">
       Mongol hordes
      </a>
      (the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dothraki_Sea" title="Dothraki Sea">
       Dothraki
      </a>
      ), as well as elements from the
      <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">
       Hundred Years' War
      </a>
      (13371453) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">
       Italian Renaissance
      </a>
      (c. 14001500).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The series' great popularity has in part been attributed to Martin's skill at fusing these disparate elements into a seamless whole that appears credible on its own terms as an alternative history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_24.2C_2013-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      "
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">
        The Sopranos
       </a>
      </i>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">
       Middle-earth
      </a>
      " is the tagline
      <a href="/wiki/Showrunner" title="Showrunner">
       showrunner
      </a>
      David Benioff jokingly suggested for
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      , referring to its intrigue-filled plot and dark tone combined with a fantasy setting that incorporates some magic and dragons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2012 study, the series was listed second out of 40 recent U.S. TV drama series by deaths per episode, with an average of 14.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cast_and_characters">
       Cast and characters
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Game_of_Thrones_characters" title="List of Game of Thrones characters">
       List of Game of Thrones characters
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con,_closeup.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="2972" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg/150px-Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg/225px-Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg/300px-Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con%2C_closeup.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Dinklage_at_the_2013_San_Diego_Comic_Con,_closeup.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">
         Peter Dinklage
        </a>
        (Tyrion Lannister) leads the principal cast from season two onwards.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Like the novels it adapts,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has a sprawling ensemble cast, estimated to be the largest on television.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the production of the third season, 257 cast names were recorded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Making_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Making-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, several of the actors' contracts were renegotiated to include the option for a seventh season, and included raises that reportedly made the cast among the best-paid on cable TV.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_30_October_2014_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter_30_October_2014-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The following overview reduces the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Game_of_Thrones_characters" title="List of Game of Thrones characters">
       list of characters in
       <i>
        Game of Thrones
       </i>
      </a>
      to those played by the actors credited as part of the main cast.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Lord
      <a href="/wiki/Ned_Stark" title="Ned Stark">
       Eddard "Ned" Stark
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bean" title="Sean Bean">
       Sean Bean
      </a>
      ) is the head of the Stark family whose members are involved in most of the series' intertwined plot lines. He and his wife
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catelyn_Tully" title="Catelyn Tully">
       Catelyn Tully
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Fairley" title="Michelle Fairley">
       Michelle Fairley
      </a>
      ) have five children: the eldest,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robb_Stark" title="Robb Stark">
       Robb
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Madden" title="Richard Madden">
       Richard Madden
      </a>
      ), the dainty
      <a href="/wiki/Sansa_Stark" title="Sansa Stark">
       Sansa
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Sophie_Turner_(actress)" title="Sophie Turner (actress)">
       Sophie Turner
      </a>
      ), the tomboy
      <a href="/wiki/Arya_Stark" title="Arya Stark">
       Arya
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Maisie_Williams" title="Maisie Williams">
       Maisie Williams
      </a>
      ), the adventurous
      <a href="/wiki/Bran_Stark" title="Bran Stark">
       Bran
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaac_Hempstead-Wright" title="Isaac Hempstead-Wright">
       Isaac Hempstead-Wright
      </a>
      ) and the youngest,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rickon_Stark" title="Rickon Stark">
       Rickon
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Art_Parkinson" title="Art Parkinson">
       Art Parkinson
      </a>
      ). Ned's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(law)" title="Legitimacy (law)">
       bastard
      </a>
      son
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_Snow_(character)" title="Jon Snow (character)">
       Jon Snow
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Kit_Harington" title="Kit Harington">
       Kit Harington
      </a>
      ) and his friend
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samwell_Tarly" title="Samwell Tarly">
       Samwell Tarly
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/John_Bradley-West" title="John Bradley-West">
       John Bradley
      </a>
      ) serve in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Night%27s_Watch" title="Night's Watch">
       Night's Watch
      </a>
      under Lord Commander
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeor_Mormont" title="Jeor Mormont">
       Jeor Mormont
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/James_Cosmo" title="James Cosmo">
       James Cosmo
      </a>
      ). The red-haired
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ygritte" title="Ygritte">
       Ygritte
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Rose_Leslie" title="Rose Leslie">
       Rose Leslie
      </a>
      ), one of the Wildlings led by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tormund_Giantsbane" title="Tormund Giantsbane">
       Tormund Giantsbane
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Kristofer_Hivju" title="Kristofer Hivju">
       Kristofer Hivju
      </a>
      ), is Jon Snow's romantic interest, and Sam cares for the young Wildling
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gilly_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Gilly (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Gilly
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Murray" title="Hannah Murray">
       Hannah Murray
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hbo_cast_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hbo_cast-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      People associated with the Starks include Ned's hostage and ward
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theon_Greyjoy" title="Theon Greyjoy">

      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Alfie_Allen" title="Alfie Allen">

      <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">

      ("bannerman")

      <a href="/wiki/Michael_McElhatton" title="Michael McElhatton">

      </a>

      </a>

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talisa_Maegyr" title="Talisa Maegyr">
       Talisa Maegyr
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Oona_Chaplin" title="Oona Chaplin">

      </a>
      ), and Arya befriends the blacksmith's apprentice
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gendry" title="Gendry">
       Gendry
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Joe_Dempsie" title="Joe Dempsie">
       Joe Dempsie
      </a>
      ) and the assassin
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaqen_H%27ghar" title="Jaqen H'ghar">
       Jaqen H'ghar
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wlaschiha" title="Tom Wlaschiha">
       Tom Wlaschiha
      </a>
      ). Catelyn encounters the tall warrior
      <a href="/wiki/Brienne_of_Tarth" title="Brienne of Tarth">
       Brienne of Tarth
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Gwendoline_Christie" title="Gwendoline Christie">

      </a>

      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hbo_cast_17-1">

      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the capital of King's Landing, Ned's old friend King
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Baratheon" title="Robert Baratheon">
       Robert Baratheon
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Addy" title="Mark Addy">
       Mark Addy
      </a>
      ) shares a loveless marriage with
      <a href="/wiki/Cersei_Lannister" title="Cersei Lannister">
       Cersei Lannister
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Lena_Headey" title="Lena Headey">
       Lena Headey
      </a>
      ), who has taken her twin, the "Kingslayer" Ser
      <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Lannister" title="Jaime Lannister">
       Jaime Lannister
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Nikolaj_Coster-Waldau" title="Nikolaj Coster-Waldau">
       Nikolaj Coster-Waldau
      </a>
      ) as her secret lover. She loathes her younger brother, the clever dwarf
      <a href="/wiki/Tyrion_Lannister" title="Tyrion Lannister">
       Tyrion
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">
       Peter Dinklage
      </a>
      ), who is attended by his mistress
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shae_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Shae (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Shae
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Sibel_Kekilli" title="Sibel Kekilli">
       Sibel Kekilli
      </a>
      ) and the sellsword
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronn_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Bronn (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Bronn
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Flynn" title="Jerome Flynn">
       Jerome Flynn
      </a>
      ). Cersei's father is the fabulously wealthy Lord
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tywin_Lannister" title="Tywin Lannister">
       Tywin
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dance" title="Charles Dance">
       Charles Dance
      </a>
      ), and she has two young sons, the cruel
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joffrey_Baratheon" title="Joffrey Baratheon">
       Joffrey
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Gleeson" title="Jack Gleeson">
       Jack Gleeson
      </a>
      ) and the kind
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tommen_Baratheon" title="Tommen Baratheon">
       Tommen
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Dean-Charles_Chapman" title="Dean-Charles Chapman">
       Dean-Charles Chapman
      </a>
      ). Joffrey is guarded by the scar-faced warrior
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandor_Clegane" title="Sandor Clegane">
       Sandor "the Hound" Clegane
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Rory_McCann" title="Rory McCann">
       Rory McCann
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hbo_cast_17-2">

        <span>

       </a>

       Petyr "Littlefinger" Baelish

      (

      ) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Eunuch" title="Eunuch">
       eunuch
      </a>
      spymaster Lord
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varys" title="Varys">
       Varys
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Conleth_Hill" title="Conleth Hill">
       Conleth Hill
      </a>
      ). Robert's brother
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stannis_Baratheon" title="Stannis Baratheon">
       Stannis Baratheon
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Dillane" title="Stephen Dillane">
       Stephen Dillane
      </a>
      ) is advised by the foreign priestess
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melisandre" title="Melisandre">
       Melisandre
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Carice_van_Houten" title="Carice van Houten">
       Carice van Houten
      </a>
      ) and the former smuggler Ser
      <a href="/wiki/Davos_Seaworth" title="Davos Seaworth">
       Davos Seaworth

      (
      <a href="/wiki/Liam_Cunningham" title="Liam Cunningham">
       Liam Cunningham
      </a>
      ). The wealthy Tyrell family is represented at court by the ambitious
      <a href="/wiki/Margaery_Tyrell" title="Margaery Tyrell">
       Margaery Tyrell
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Dormer" title="Natalie Dormer">

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellaria_Sand" title="Ellaria Sand">
       Ellaria Sand
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Indira_Varma" title="Indira Varma">
       Indira Varma
      </a>
      ) seeks vengeance against the Lannisters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hbo_cast_17-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-hbo_cast-17">
        <span>

        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Across the Narrow Sea, siblings
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viserys_Targaryen" title="Viserys Targaryen">
       Viserys

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khal_Drogo" title="Khal Drogo">

      </a>
      ) and the sellsword

       Daario Naharis
      </a>
      (

       Michiel Huisman

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
       Production
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_1)" title="Game of Thrones (season 1)">
       Season 1
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_2)" title="Game of Thrones (season 2)">
       Season 2
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_3)" title="Game of Thrones (season 3)">
       Season 3
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_4)" title="Game of Thrones (season 4)">
       Season 4
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_5)" title="Game of Thrones (season 5)">
       Season 5
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conception_and_development">
       Conception and development
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="513" data-file-width="660" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg/220px-D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg/330px-D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg/440px-D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:D._B._Weiss_and_David_Benioff.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Showrunner" title="Showrunner">
         Showrunners
        </a>
        D. B. Weiss and David Benioff created the series, wrote most of its episodes and directed some of them.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to David Benioff and D. B. Weiss, the two came up with the idea of adapting George R. R. Martin's novels to the screen in 2006, after Benioff began reading the first novel,
      <i>
       A Game of Thrones
      </i>
      . He called Weiss to share his excitement, and Weiss finished the thousand-page novel in "maybe 36 hours".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upclose20130508_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-upclose20130508-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They successfully
      <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(filmmaking)" title="Pitch (filmmaking)">
       pitched
      </a>
      the series to HBO, and convinced Martin  a veteran screenwriter himself  in the course of a five-hour meeting in a restaurant on
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica_Boulevard" title="Santa Monica Boulevard">
       Santa Monica Boulevard
      </a>
      to agree to the idea. Benioff recalled they won Martin over with their answer to his question: "Who is
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_Snow_(character)" title="Jon Snow (character)">
       Jon Snow
      </a>
      's mother?"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upclose20130508_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-upclose20130508-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The series began development in January 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-var_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-var-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HBO, after acquiring the TV rights to the novels, hired Benioff and Weiss to write and executive produce the series, which would cover one novel's worth of material per season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-var_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-var-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Initially, Benioff and Weiss were to write every episode, save one per season, which Martin, who also joined as a co-executive producer, was attached to write.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-var_19-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-var-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jane_Espenson" title="Jane Espenson">
       Jane Espenson
      </a>
      and Bryan Cogman were later added to each write one episode of the first season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gotfactsheet_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-gotfactsheet-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first and second drafts of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilot_episode" title="Pilot episode">
       pilot
      </a>
      script, written by Benioff and Weiss, were submitted in August 2007
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and June 2008,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOB_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NOB-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      respectively. While HBO found both drafts to their liking,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOB_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NOB-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewq.26a_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ewq.26a-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a pilot was not ordered until November 2008,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" title="20072008 Writers Guild of America strike">
       20072008 Writers Guild of America strike
      </a>
      possibly delaying the process.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewq.26a_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ewq.26a-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The pilot reportedly cost HBO between
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$5 and 10 million
      </span>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the total budget for the first season had been estimated at
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$5060 million
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the second season, the show obtained a 15% budget increase to depict the climactic battle in the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Blackwater_(Game_of_Thrones)" title="Blackwater (Game of Thrones)">
       Blackwater
      </a>
      ", which had a budget of
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$8 million
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between 2012 and 2015, the average episode's budget grew from
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$6 million
      </span>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to "at least" 8 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_March_2015_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW_March_2015-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">
       Writing
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1639" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg/170px-George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg/255px-George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg/340px-George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:George_R.R._Martin_at_Archipelacon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        George R. R. Martin, the author of
        <i>
         A Song of Ice and Fire
        </i>
        , is attached to the series as a co-
        <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">
         executive producer
        </a>
        and wrote one episode for each of the first four seasons.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has used seven writers over the course of five seasons. Series creators
      <a href="/wiki/David_Benioff" title="David Benioff">
       David Benioff
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/D._B._Weiss" title="D. B. Weiss">
       D. B. Weiss
      </a>
      are the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Showrunners" title="Showrunners">
       showrunners
      </a>
      and write the majority of the episodes each season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-observer-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">
        A Song of Ice and Fire
       </a>
      </i>
      author
      <a href="/wiki/George_R._R._Martin" title="George R. R. Martin">
       George R. R. Martin
      </a>
      wrote one episode in each of the first four seasons, but has not written an episode for the fifth or sixth seasons, as Martin wants to focus on completing the sixth novel,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Winds_of_Winter" title="The Winds of Winter">
        The Winds of Winter
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jane_Espenson" title="Jane Espenson">
       Jane Espenson
      </a>
      co-wrote one episode for the first season as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freelance_writer" title="Freelance writer">
       freelance writer
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espenson_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-espenson-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Cogman" title="Bryan Cogman">
       Bryan Cogman
      </a>
      , who initially was a script coordinator for the series,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espenson_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-espenson-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was promoted to a producer beginning with the fifth season. Cogman wrote at least one episode for the first five seasons, and is the only other writer to be in the writers' room with Benioff and Weiss; besides
      <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Taylor" title="Vanessa Taylor">
       Vanessa Taylor
      </a>
      , who was a writer during the second and third seasons. Dave Hill joined the writing staff for the fifth season after previously working as an assistant to Benioff and Weiss.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Martin is not in the writers' room, but reads the script outlines and gives notes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-observer-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Benioff and Weiss sometimes assign various characters to each writer; for example, Cogman was assigned Arya for the fourth season. From there, the writers spend a few weeks writing a character outline, including what material from the novels to use and what the themes are. After the individual outlines are complete, the writers spend another two-to-three weeks discussing each main character's individual arc, and arrange them episode-by-episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_31-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-observer-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From there, a detailed outline is created and each of the writers work on a portion of it, to create a script for each episode. Cogman, who wrote two episodes for the fifth season, took a month and a half to complete both scripts. The scripts are then read by Benioff and Weiss, who give notes, and then parts of script are rewritten. All ten episodes are written before filming begins, as all the episodes are filmed simultaneously, out of order, and using two separate
      <a href="/wiki/Film_crew" title="Film crew">
       units
      </a>
      in different countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_31-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-observer-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Adaptation_schedule">
       Adaptation schedule
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Showrunner" title="Showrunner">
       Showrunners
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Benioff" title="David Benioff">
       David Benioff
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/D._B._Weiss" title="D. B. Weiss">
       D. B. Weiss
      </a>
      intend to adapt the entirety of the still incomplete
      <i>
       A Song of Ice and Fire
      </i>
      novel series. In 2013, they envisioned the series to have a scope of some 80 hours, about eight seasons' worth of material.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2015, Benioff and Weiss said that with the fifth season adapting all material from the novels published so far,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      might begin outpacing
      <i>
       A Song of Ice and Fire
      </i>
      in the sixth season. The series would then be based on an outline of the plot of the future novels provided by Martin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2015, six seasons have been ordered and five have been filmed, adapting the novels at a rate of about 0.8 minutes per page for the first three seasons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable">
