     </table>
     <p>
      Seasons 1 and 2 each adapted one novel. For the later seasons, the creators conceive of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      as an adaptation of
      <i>
       A Song of Ice and Fire
      </i>
      as a whole, rather than of individual novels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This gives them the liberty to move events back and forth across novels according to the requirements of the screen adaptation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW.com_March_30.2C_2012_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW.com_March_30.2C_2012-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The five seasons filmed so far each consist of ten episodes, with an average runtime of 55 minutes per episode. The series' pilot and every season finale, bar the first, run for more than an hour apiece.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">
       Filming
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dubrovnik_crop.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1434" data-file-width="1714" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Dubrovnik_crop.jpg/220px-Dubrovnik_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Dubrovnik_crop.jpg/330px-Dubrovnik_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Dubrovnik_crop.jpg/440px-Dubrovnik_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dubrovnik_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Walls_of_Dubrovnik" title="Walls of Dubrovnik">
         walled city
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">
         Dubrovnik
        </a>
        stands in for King's Landing from season2 onwards
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg/220px-Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg/330px-Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg/440px-Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ballintoy_Harbour_-_geograph.org.uk_-_19750.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballintoy_Harbour" title="Ballintoy Harbour">
         Ballintoy Harbour
        </a>
        was redressed as Lordsport on the Iron Islands
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malta191.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta191.jpg/220px-Malta191.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta191.jpg/330px-Malta191.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta191.jpg/440px-Malta191.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malta191.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Azure_Window" title="Azure Window">
         Azure Window
        </a>
        in Malta was the site of the Dothraki wedding in season 1.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Principal photography for the first season was scheduled to begin on July 26, 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gotfactsheet_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-gotfactsheet-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The primary location was the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Paint_Hall" title="The Paint Hall">
       Paint Hall Studios
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">
       Belfast
      </a>
      , Northern Ireland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Exterior scenes in Northern Ireland were filmed at Sandy Brae in the
      <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Mountains" title="Mourne Mountains">
       Mourne Mountains
      </a>
      (standing in for Vaes Dothrak),
      <a href="/wiki/Castle_Ward" title="Castle Ward">
       Castle Ward
      </a>
      (Winterfell), Saintfield Estates (the Winterfell godswood),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tollymore_Forest" title="Tollymore Forest">
       Tollymore Forest
      </a>
      (outdoor scenes),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cairncastle" title="Cairncastle">
       Cairncastle
      </a>
      (the execution site),
      <a href="/wiki/Magheramorne" title="Magheramorne">
       Magheramorne
      </a>
      quarry (Castle Black) and at
      <a href="/wiki/Shane%27s_Castle" title="Shane's Castle">
       Shane's Castle
      </a>
      (the tourney grounds).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Doune_Castle" title="Doune Castle">
       Doune Castle
      </a>
      in Stirling, Scotland, was also used in the original pilot episode for exterior and interior scenes at Winterfell.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The producers initially considered shooting the whole series in Scotland, but eventually chose Northern Ireland because of the availability of studio space.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first season's southern scenes were filmed in
      <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
       Malta
      </a>
      , a change in location from the sets in
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      used for the pilot episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gotfactsheet_2-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-gotfactsheet-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city of
      <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">
       Mdina
      </a>
      was used for scenes in King's Landing, and filming also took place at
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Manoel" title="Fort Manoel">
       Fort Manoel
      </a>
      (representing the Sept of Baelor), at the
      <a href="/wiki/Azure_Window" title="Azure Window">
       Azure Window
      </a>
      on the island of
      <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">
       Gozo
      </a>
      (the Dothraki wedding site), and at
      <a href="/wiki/San_Anton_Palace" title="San Anton Palace">
       San Anton Palace
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ricasoli" title="Fort Ricasoli">
       Fort Ricasoli
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_St_Angelo" title="Fort St Angelo">
       Fort St Angelo
      </a>
      and St. Dominic monastery (all used for scenes in the Red Keep).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For the second season, shooting of the Southern scenes shifted from Malta to
      <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
       Croatia
      </a>
      , where the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">
       Dubrovnik
      </a>
      and nearby locations allowed exterior shots of a seaside walled medieval city. The
      <a href="/wiki/Walls_of_Dubrovnik" title="Walls of Dubrovnik">
       Walls of Dubrovnik
      </a>
      and of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Lovrijenac" title="Fort Lovrijenac">
       Fort Lovrijenac
      </a>
      were used for scenes in King's Landing and the Red Keep. The island of
      <a href="/wiki/Lokrum" title="Lokrum">
       Lokrum
      </a>
      , the St. Dominic monastery in the coastal town of
      <a href="/wiki/Trogir" title="Trogir">
       Trogir
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Rector%27s_Palace,_Dubrovnik" title="Rector's Palace, Dubrovnik">
       Rector's Palace
      </a>
      in Dubrovnik and the Dubac quarry a few kilometers to the east were used for scenes set in Qarth. Scenes set north of the Wall, in the Frostfangs and at the Fist of the First Men, were filmed in
      <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">
       Iceland
      </a>
      in November 2011, on the Svnafellsjkull glacier and near Smyrlabjrg and
      <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADk_%C3%AD_M%C3%BDrdal" title="Vk  Mrdal">
       Vk
      </a>
      on Hfabrekkuheii.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012_1-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_March_30.2C_2012-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For the third season the production returned to
      <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">
       Dubrovnik
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
       Croatia
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Walls_of_Dubrovnik" title="Walls of Dubrovnik">
       Walls of Dubrovnik
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Lovrijenac" title="Fort Lovrijenac">
       Fort Lovrijenac
      </a>
      and nearby locations were used for scenes in King's Landing and the Red Keep. One new location
      <a href="/wiki/Trsteno_Arboretum" title="Trsteno Arboretum">
       Trsteno Arboretum
      </a>
      is the garden the Tyrells use in King's Landing. The third season also returned to
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      (previously used in the pilot episode), including the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">
       Essaouira
      </a>
      , to film Daenerys' scenes in Essos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The production employed three units ("Dragon", "Wolf" and "Raven") filming in parallel, six directing teams, 257 cast members and 703 crew members.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Making_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Making-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One scene with
      <a href="/wiki/Bart_the_Bear_2" title="Bart the Bear 2">
       a live bear
      </a>
      was filmed in
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gotlosangeles_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gotlosangeles-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fourth season returned to Dubrovnik and included new locations in Croatia, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Diocletian%27s_Palace" title="Diocletian's Palace">
       Diocletian's Palace
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Split,_Croatia" title="Split, Croatia">
       Split
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Klis_Fortress" title="Klis Fortress">
       Klis Fortress
      </a>
      north of Split, Perun quarry east of Split,
      <a href="/wiki/Mosor" title="Mosor">
       Mosor
      </a>
      mountain and
      <a href="/wiki/Ba%C5%A1ka_Voda" title="Baka Voda">
       Baka Voda
      </a>
      further down to the south.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Filming took 136 days, ending on November 21, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fifth season added
      <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
       Seville
      </a>
      , Spain, as a filming location, which is used for the fictional location of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorne" title="Dorne">
       Dorne
      </a>
      . The sixth season, which will begin filming in July 2015, will return to Spain, and film in the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Girona" title="Girona">
       Girona
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%ADscola" title="Pescola">
       Pescola
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Costuming">
       Costuming
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte,_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2316" data-file-width="3592" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg/220px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg/330px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg/440px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte%2C_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Ygritte,_Jon_and_Tormund_costumes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The costumes of Ygritte, Jon Snow and Tormund Giantsbane reflect the harsh climate in which they are worn.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2686" data-file-width="5184" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg/220px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg/330px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg/440px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Royal_court_costumes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The rich dresses worn at the royal court in King's Landing advertise their wearers' wealth and status.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3293" data-file-width="2836" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg/220px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg/330px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg/440px-Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_Oslo_exhibition_2014_-_Brienne_and_Jaime_costumes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Functional weapons and armor, like
        <a href="/wiki/Brienne_of_Tarth" title="Brienne of Tarth">
         Brienne of Tarth
        </a>
        's (left), were manufactured for the series.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The show's costumes are inspired by many cultures, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_armor" title="Japanese armor">
       Japanese
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_clothing" title="Persian clothing">
       Persian
      </a>
      . Dothraki outfits resemble the
      <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">
       Bedouin
      </a>
      's (one was made out of fish skins to resemble dragon scales), and the Wildlings wear animal skins inside out like the
      <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">
       Inuit
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wischhover20120604_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wischhover20120604-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Wildling bone armor is made of molds taken of real bones and assembled with string and latex resembling
      <a href="/wiki/Catgut" title="Catgut">
       catgut
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snead20120611_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-snead20120611-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While extras who portray Wildlings and the Night's Watch wear hats as would be normal in a cold climate, main actors usually do not so viewers can identify the characters.
      <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk" title="Bjrk">
       Bjrk
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_McQueen" title="Alexander McQueen">
       Alexander McQueen
      </a>
      high-neckline dresses inspired Dormer's unusual funnel-neck outfit, and prostitute costumes are designed to be quickly removed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wischhover20120604_55-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-wischhover20120604-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All clothing, whether for Wildlings or for women at the royal court, is aged for two weeks to improve realism on high-definition television.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snead20120611_56-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-snead20120611-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      About two dozen wigs are used for the actresses. Made of human hair and up to 2 feet (61cm) in length, they cost up to $7,000 each and are washed and styled like real hair. Applying the wigs is a lengthy process; Clarke, for example, requires about two hours to style her brunette hair with a platinum-blonde wig and braids. Other actors such as Gleeson and Turner receive frequent haircoloring. For characters such as Daenerys (Clarke) and her Dothraki, hair, wigs, and costumes are processed so they appear as if they have not been washed for weeks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wischhover20120604_55-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-wischhover20120604-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_effects">
       Visual effects
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      For the large amount of visual effects in the series, HBO hired the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VFX" title="VFX">
       VFX
      </a>
      companies BlueBolt, based in Great Britain, and Screen Scene, based in Ireland, for season one. Most of the environment builds were done as
      <a href="/wiki/2.5D" title="2.5D">
       2.5D
      </a>
      projections, to give the viewer a good sense of perspective, but also to keep the amount of programming from becoming too overwhelming.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vfx-got_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vfx-got-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The season one finale "
      <a href="/wiki/Fire_and_Blood_(Game_of_Thrones)" title="Fire and Blood (Game of Thrones)">
       Fire and Blood
      </a>
      " was nominated for an
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Special_Visual_Effects" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Special Visual Effects">
       Emmy Award for Visual Effects
      </a>
      in 2011.
     </p>
     <p>
      Because the effects became more complex in the subsequent seasons, including
      <a href="/wiki/Computer_graphics" title="Computer graphics">
       CG
      </a>
      creatures, fire, and water, the job was passed on to
      <a href="/wiki/Pixomondo" title="Pixomondo">
       Pixomondo
      </a>
      of Germany. Starting with the second season, Pixomondo served as lead VFX producer. For season two, nine of its twelve facilities contributed to the project, with Stuttgart serving as the lead.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, some scenes were produced by Peanut FX (Great Britain), Spin VFX (Canada) and Gradient Effects (U.S.). The episodes "
      <a href="/wiki/Valar_Morghulis" title="Valar Morghulis">
       Valar Morghulis
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Valar_Dohaeris" title="Valar Dohaeris">
       Valar Dohaeris
      </a>
      " earned Pixomondo the Emmy Award for Visual Effects in 2012 and 2013, respectively.
     </p>
     <p>
      For season four, HBO added Mackevision, also based in Germany, to the project.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mckvsn_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mckvsn-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The season four finale "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Children_(Game_of_Thrones)" title="The Children (Game of Thrones)">
       The Children
      </a>
      " won the Emmy Award for Visual Effects in 2014. Additional producers for season four included
      <a href="/wiki/Rodeo_FX" title="Rodeo FX">
       Rodeo FX
      </a>
      (Canada),
      <a href="/wiki/Scanline_VFX" title="Scanline VFX">
       Scanline VFX
      </a>
      (Germany) and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAKED_FX" title="BAKED FX">
       BAKED FX
      </a>
      (U.S.). The muscle and wing movements of the adolescent dragons in seasons 4 and 5 were based largely on those of a chicken. Pixomondo retained a team of 22 to 30 people, focusing solely on the visualization of Daenerys Targaryens dragons, with the average production time per season ranging between 20 and 22 weeks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the fifth season, HBO also added
      <a href="/wiki/Image_Engine" title="Image Engine">
       Image Engine
      </a>
      (Canada) and Crazy Horse Effects (U.S.) to its list of main VFX producers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sound">
       Sound
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Unusually for television shows, the sound team receives a rough-cut of a full season to work on, and they approach it like a ten-hour feature film. Season 1 and 2 each had a different sound team, but for the subsequent seasons, the same team has been working on the sound.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the show's blood and gore sounds, the sound team often uses a
      <a href="/wiki/Chamois_leather" title="Chamois leather">
       shammy
      </a>
      . For dragon screams, they have used the sounds of two tortoises mating, as well as dolphin, seal, lion and bird sounds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Title_sequence">
       Title sequence
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_title_sequence" title="Game of Thrones title sequence">
       Game of Thrones title sequence
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The series'
      <a href="/wiki/Title_sequence" title="Title sequence">
       title sequence
      </a>
      was created by production studio Elastic for HBO.
      <a href="/wiki/Creative_director" title="Creative director">
       Creative director
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Angus_Wall" title="Angus Wall">
       Angus Wall
      </a>
      and his collaborators received the 2011
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Main_Title_Design" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Main Title Design">
       Emmy Award for Main Title Design
      </a>
      for their work on the sequence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Hollywood_Reporter_September_10.2C_2011_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Hollywood_Reporter_September_10.2C_2011-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It depicts a
      <a href="/wiki/Raised-relief_map" title="Raised-relief map">
       three-dimensional map
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/World_of_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="World of A Song of Ice and Fire">
       the series' fictional world
      </a>
      , projected onto the inside of a sphere, which is centrally lit by a small sun contained within an
      <a href="/wiki/Armillary_sphere" title="Armillary sphere">
       armilla
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Art_of_the_Title_2013_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Art_of_the_Title_2013-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As the camera swoops across the map and focuses on the locations in which the episode's events take place, complex clockwork mechanisms let buildings and other structures emerge from the map and unfold. Meanwhile, accompanied by the
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Game_of_Thrones" title="Music of Game of Thrones">
       title music
      </a>
      , the names of the principal cast and creative staff are displayed. The sequence concludes after about one and a half minutes with the title card and brief
      <a href="/wiki/Opening_credits" title="Opening credits">
       opening credits
      </a>
      indicating the episode's writer(s) and director. The composition of the title sequence changes as the story progresses, as new places are introduced they replace others that no longer feature as prominently or at all.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Art_of_the_Title_2013_67-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Art_of_the_Title_2013-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
       Language
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Westerosi characters of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      speak
      <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">
       British English
      </a>
      , often (but not consistently) with the accent of the English region whose geographic location corresponds to the character's Westerosi region. For instance, Eddard Stark, as Warden of the North, speaks in actor Sean Bean's native
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yorkshire_accent" title="Yorkshire accent">
       northern accent
      </a>
      , while the southern lord Tywin Lannister speaks with a
      <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">
       southern accent
      </a>
      . Characters foreign to Westeros are often (although not always) played with a non-British accent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While English is used to convey the common language of Westeros, the producers charged linguist
      <a href="/wiki/David_J._Peterson" title="David J. Peterson">
       David J. Peterson
      </a>
      with developing the
      <a href="/wiki/Dothraki_language" title="Dothraki language">
       Dothraki
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Valyrian_languages" title="Valyrian languages">
       Valyrian languages
      </a>
      as
      <a href="/wiki/Constructed_language" title="Constructed language">
       constructed languages
      </a>
      , based on the few words used in Martin's novels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vulture_April_23.2C_2013_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Vulture_April_23.2C_2013-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Dothraki or Valyrian dialogue is subtitled in English. The BBC estimated that, through the series, these fictional languages were heard by more people than the
      <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">
       Welsh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">
       Irish
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots_Gaelic" title="Scots Gaelic">
       Scots Gaelic
      </a>
      languages combined.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_location">
       Effect on location
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      receives funding from
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Screen" title="Northern Ireland Screen">
       Northern Ireland Screen
      </a>
      , a government agency financed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invest_NI" title="Invest NI">
       Invest NI
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Regional_Development_Fund" title="European Regional Development Fund">
       European Regional Development Fund
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of April 2013, Northern Ireland Screen has awarded the show 9.25 million and according to government estimates, benefited the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_economy" title="Northern Ireland economy">
       Northern Ireland economy
      </a>
      by 65 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bradley20120412_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bradley20120412-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_Ireland" title="Tourism Ireland">
       Tourism Ireland
      </a>
      has a
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      -themed marketing campaign similar to
      <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">
       New Zealand
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Tolkien_tourism" title="Tolkien tourism">
       Tolkien-related advertising
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shankman20140406_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-shankman20140406-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Invest NI and the
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Tourist_Board" title="Northern Ireland Tourist Board">
       Tourist Board
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bradley20120412_74-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-bradley20120412-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      also expect the series to generate tourism revenue. According to a government minister, the series has given Northern Ireland the most publicity in its history outside politics and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">
       the Troubles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The production of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      and other TV series has also provided a boost to the creative industry in Northern Ireland, contributing to a growth of 12.4% in arts, entertainment and recreation jobs from 2008 to 2013 (as opposed to 4.3% in the whole of the UK).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Tourism organizations in other filming locations also reported notable increases in bookings after their locations appeared in
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      . Bookings through one web portal in 2012 increased by 13% in Iceland and by 28% in
      <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">
       Dubrovnik
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
       Croatia
      </a>
      . In 2013, bookings increased by 100% in
      <a href="/wiki/Ouarzazate" title="Ouarzazate">
       Ouarzazate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      , where Daenerys' season 3 scenes were filmed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Availability">
       Availability
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">
       Broadcast
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      is broadcast by
      <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">
       HBO
      </a>
      in the United States, and through its local subsidiaries or other
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pay_TV" title="Pay TV">
       pay TV
      </a>
      services in other countries, either at the same time as in the U.S. or some weeks or months later. The series' broadcast in China on
      <a href="/wiki/China_Central_Television" title="China Central Television">
       CCTV
      </a>
      , beginning in 2014, was heavily edited to remove scenes of sex and violence, in accordance with a Chinese practice of censoring western TV series to prevent "negative effects and hidden security dangers", according to the
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People's Daily">
       People's Daily
      </a>
      . This resulted in viewer complaints about the incoherence of what remained of the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Broadcasters carrying
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      include
      <a href="/wiki/Showcase_(Australian_TV_channel)" title="Showcase (Australian TV channel)">
       Showcase
      </a>
      in Australia,
      <a href="/wiki/HBO_Canada" title="HBO Canada">
       HBO Canada
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Super_%C3%89cran" title="Super cran">
       Super cran
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Showcase_(Canadian_TV_channel)" title="Showcase (Canadian TV channel)">
       Showcase
      </a>
      in Canada,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soho_(New_Zealand)" title="Soho (New Zealand)">
       SoHo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Prime_(New_Zealand)" title="Prime (New Zealand)">
       Prime
      </a>
      in New Zealand, and
      <a href="/wiki/Sky_Atlantic" title="Sky Atlantic">
       Sky Atlantic
      </a>
      in the United Kingdom and Ireland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Home_video">
       Home video
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The ten episodes of the first season of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      were published as a DVD and
      <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">
       Blu-ray
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">
       box set
      </a>
      on March 6, 2012. The set includes extra background and behind-the-scenes material, but no deleted scenes, because almost all the footage shot for the first season was used in the show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The box set sold 350,000 units in the first seven days of its release, the largest first-week DVD sales ever for an HBO series. The series also set an HBO series record for digital download sales.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A "collector's edition" of the box set combining the DVD and Blu-ray versions, a dragon's egg paperweight and the first episode of season two was released in November 2012.
     </p>
     <p>
      DVD/Blu-ray box sets and digital downloads of the second season were made available on February 19, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      First-day sales again broke HBO records, with 241,000 box sets sold and 355,000 episodes downloaded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The third season was made available for purchase as a digital download on the
      <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">
       iTunes Store
      </a>
      , in Australia only, in parallel to the U.S. premiere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Piracy">
       Piracy
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      is notorious for being widely
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement_of_audio-visual_works" title="Copyright infringement of audio-visual works">
       pirated
      </a>
      , mainly outside the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_9_April_2015_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-THR_9_April_2015-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      File-sharing news website
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/TorrentFreak" title="TorrentFreak">
        TorrentFreak
       </a>
      </i>
      estimated
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      to be the most-pirated TV series every year since 2012,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and illegal downloads grew to about 7 million in the first quarter of 2015, up 45% from 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_9_April_2015_86-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-THR_9_April_2015-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One episode was downloaded about 4,280,000 times through public
      <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_tracker" title="BitTorrent tracker">
       BitTorrent trackers
      </a>
      in 2012, about equal to the number of broadcast viewers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Piracy rates were particularly high in Australia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This led U.S. Ambassador to Australia
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeff_Bleich" title="Jeff Bleich">
       Jeff Bleich
      </a>
      to issue a public statement
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      condemning Australian piracy of the series in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The delays in availability outside of HBO or its affiliates
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      encountered prior to 2015 and the cost of subscriptions to these services have been pointed to as causes of the series' widespread illegal distribution. According to
      <i>
       TorrentFreak
      </i>
      , this cost ranges from 15 to 25 U.S. dollars per month in the U.S. up to 26 pounds per episode in the UK and 52 Australian dollars per episode in Australia, if somebody were to subscribe to a service exclusively for
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To counteract piracy, HBO said in 2013 it intended to make its content more widely available within the week of the U.S. premiere, including through
      <a href="/wiki/HBO_Go" title="HBO Go">
       HBO Go
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in 2015 the fifth season was
      <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">
       simulcast
      </a>
      to 170 countries as well as
      <a href="/wiki/HBO_Now" title="HBO Now">
       HBO Now
      </a>
      users.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_9_April_2015_86-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-THR_9_April_2015-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on April 11, 2015, the day before the season premiere,
      <a href="/wiki/Screener" title="Screener">
       screener
      </a>
      copies of the first four episodes of the fifth season leaked to numerous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/File-sharing" title="File-sharing">
       file-sharing
      </a>
      websites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Within the first day after the leak, the files had been downloaded at least 800,000 times,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in just one week the figure reached a total of 32 million in illegal downloads, with the season five premiere episode "The Wars to Come" pirated 13 million times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The season five finale, "
      <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Mercy" title="Mother's Mercy">
       Mother's Mercy
      </a>
      ", was the most simultaneously shared file in the history of the
      <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent" title="BitTorrent">
       BitTorrent
      </a>
      filesharing protocol, with over 250,000 simultaneous sharers and over 1.5 million downloads within 8 hours.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Observers, including series director
      <a href="/wiki/David_Petrarca" title="David Petrarca">
       David Petrarca
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" title="Time Warner">
       Time Warner
      </a>
      CEO
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeff_Bewkes" title="Jeff Bewkes">
       Jeff Bewkes
      </a>
      said illegal downloads did not hurt the series' prospects, as it benefited from the resulting "
      <a href="/wiki/Marketing_buzz" title="Marketing buzz">
       buzz
      </a>
      " and social commentary, while the high rates of piracy did not significantly translate to lost subscriptions. According to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Polygon_(website)" title="Polygon (website)">
        Polygon
       </a>
      </i>
      , HBO's relatively relaxed attitude towards piracy and sharing login credentials amounted to a "
      <a href="/wiki/Free-to-play" title="Free-to-play">
       free-to-play
      </a>
      " model for premium television.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Polygon_April_21.2C_2014_103-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Polygon_April_21.2C_2014-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At a debate at the
      <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Union" title="Oxford Union">
       Oxford Union
      </a>
      in 2015, series co-creator David Benioff stated he was just glad people are watching the show. He claimed that the illegaly downloaded copies of the show sometimes captivate viewers enough to make them eventually buy a copy of the show later on anyway, especially in countries where the show does not officially air on television. D. B. Weiss responded with mixed feelings, saying the show costs a lot of money to produce and "if it doesn't make the money back, then it ceases to exist" but on the other hand also enjoying the fact that many people "enjoy the show so much they can't wait to get their hands on it."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="IMAX">
       IMAX
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Beginning January 23, 2015, the last two episodes of
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_4)" title="Game of Thrones (season 4)">
       season four
      </a>
      were shown in 205
      <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">
       IMAX
      </a>
      theaters in the U.S.
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      is the first TV series released in this format.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The show earned $686,000 in its opening day at the box office
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and $1.5 million during its opening weekend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media_and_products">
       Other media and products
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">
       Soundtrack
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Game_of_Thrones" title="Music of Game of Thrones">
       Music of Game of Thrones
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The music for the series is composed by
      <a href="/wiki/Ramin_Djawadi" title="Ramin Djawadi">
       Ramin Djawadi
      </a>
      . The first season's soundtrack, written in about ten weeks before the show's premiere,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ryan_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ryan-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was published by
      <a href="/wiki/Var%C3%A8se_Sarabande" title="Varse Sarabande">
       Varse Sarabande
      </a>
      in June 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Soundtrack albums for the subsequent seasons have also been published, featuring tracks performed by the bands
      <a href="/wiki/The_National_(band)" title="The National (band)">
       The National
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Hold_Steady" title="The Hold Steady">
       The Hold Steady
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sigur_R%C3%B3s" title="Sigur Rs">
       Sigur Rs
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The series' instrumental title music has been
      <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">
       covered
      </a>
      numerous times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired-15-04-2013_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wired-15-04-2013-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Lyrics were added for the first time in 2014, when
      <a href="/wiki/%22Weird_Al%22_Yankovic" title='"Weird Al" Yankovic'>
       "Weird Al" Yankovic
      </a>
      performed a parody version during the
      <a href="/wiki/66th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="66th Primetime Emmy Awards">
       66th Primetime Emmy Awards
      </a>
      presentation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parody_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-parody-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/Forte_Tenors" title="Forte Tenors">
       Forte Tenors
      </a>
      added lyrics based on
      <a href="/wiki/Valyrian_languages#High_Valyrian" title="Valyrian languages">
       High Valyrian
      </a>
      text for their
      <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">
       operatic
      </a>
      performance and music video, released in March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoT-Forte_112-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GoT-Forte-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Accompanying_material">
       Accompanying material
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Thronecast: The Official Guide to Game of Thrones
      </i>
      , a series of
      <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">
       podcasts
      </a>
      presented by
      <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Lloyd" title="Geoff Lloyd">
       Geoff Lloyd
      </a>
      and produced by Koink, was released on the
      <a href="/wiki/Sky_Atlantic" title="Sky Atlantic">
       Sky Atlantic
      </a>
      website and the UK
      <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">
       iTunes
      </a>
      store. A new podcast was released after each episode, featuring analysis and cast interviews.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thronecast_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Thronecast-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 2015,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HBO commissioned free albums of rap songs about the series, called
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catch_the_Throne" title="Catch the Throne">
        Catch the Throne
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      A companion book,
      <i>
       Inside HBO's Game of Thrones
      </i>
      by series writer
      <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Cogman" title="Bryan Cogman">
       Bryan Cogman
      </a>
      (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781452110103">
       ISBN 978-1-4521-1010-3
      </a>
      ), was published on September 27, 2012. On 192 pages, illustrated with concept art and behind-the-scenes photographs, the book covers the creation of the series' first two seasons, as well as its principal characters and families.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise_and_exhibition">
       Merchandise and exhibition
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg/220px-Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg/330px-Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg/440px-Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Game_of_Thrones_merchandise_in_HBO_shop.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A selection of
        <i>
         Game of Thrones
        </i>
        merchandise sold in HBO's New York City store
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      HBO has issued licenses for a broad range of
      <a href="/wiki/Merchandising#Licensing" title="Merchandising">
       merchandise
      </a>
      based on
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      . These include
      <a href="/wiki/Works_based_on_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire#Games" title="Works based on A Song of Ice and Fire">
       various games
      </a>
      , replica weapons and armor, jewellery,
      <a href="/wiki/Bobblehead" title="Bobblehead">
       bobblehead
      </a>
      dolls by
      <a href="/wiki/Funko" title="Funko">
       Funko
      </a>
      , beer by
      <a href="/wiki/Brewery_Ommegang" title="Brewery Ommegang">
       Ommegang
      </a>
      , and various items and apparel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Top-end merchandise includes
      <a href="/wiki/Ulysse_Nardin" title="Ulysse Nardin">
       Ulysse Nardin
      </a>
      wristwatches for $10,500
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Resin" title="Resin">
       resin
      </a>
      replicas of the
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Throne_(A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire)" title="Iron Throne (A Song of Ice and Fire)">
       Iron Throne
      </a>
      for $30,000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2013 and 2014, a traveling exhibition of costumes, props, armor and weapons from the series visited several major cities in Europe and the Americas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works_based_on_the_series">
       Other works based on the series
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Works_based_on_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="Works based on A Song of Ice and Fire">
       Works based on A Song of Ice and Fire
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The series has also inspired other works, including
      <a href="/wiki/Works_based_on_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire#Video_games" title="Works based on A Song of Ice and Fire">
       four video games
      </a>
      based on the TV series and novels. The strategy game
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_Ascent" title="Game of Thrones Ascent">
        Game of Thrones Ascent
       </a>
      </i>
      ties in particularly closely with the series, making characters and settings available to players as soon as they appear on air.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fall 2012
      <a href="/wiki/Ready-to-wear" title="Ready-to-wear">
       ready-to-wear
      </a>
      collection by the fashion brand
      <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Lang_(fashion_brand)" title="Helmut Lang (fashion brand)">
       Helmut Lang
      </a>
      was inspired by
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/Wiley-Blackwell" title="Wiley-Blackwell">
       Wiley-Blackwell
      </a>
      published
      <i>
       Game of Thrones and Philosophy: Logic Cuts Deeper than the Sword
      </i>
      (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781118161999">
       ISBN 978-1-118-16199-9
      </a>
      ). This entry in Blackwell's
      <i>
       Pop Culture and Philosophy
      </i>
      series, edited by Henry Jacoby and
      <a href="/wiki/William_Irwin_(philosopher)" title="William Irwin (philosopher)">
       William Irwin
      </a>
      , aims to highlight and discuss philosophical issues raised by the show and its source material.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2013,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      was notably parodied on the cover of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mad_(magazine)" title="Mad (magazine)">
        Mad
       </a>
      </i>
      on April 30,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as well as by a
      <a href="/wiki/Web_series" title="Web series">
       web series
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       School of Thrones
      </i>
      , which set the story in a high school whose students vie for the title of
      <a href="/wiki/Prom" title="Prom">
       prom
      </a>
      king and queen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two
      <a href="/wiki/Pornographic_parody_film" title="Pornographic parody film">
       pornographic parodies
      </a>
      of the series were also announced in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The "One World Symphony" company announced, in 2014, a musical production based on television series including
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2015, the
      <a href="/wiki/Under_the_Gun_Theater" title="Under the Gun Theater">
       Under the Gun Theater
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      premiered
      <i>
       Swarm of Spoilers
      </i>
      , a parody show recapitulating the first four seasons of the TV series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
       Reception
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      was highly anticipated by fans before its premiere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has since become a critical and commercial success. By 2014, according to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">
        The Guardian
       </a>
      </i>
      it had become "the biggest drama" and "the most talked about show" on television.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_influence">
       Cultural influence
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Although the series was dismissed or patronizingly reviewed by some critics prior to being aired on account of its genre trappings,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014_132-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      its subsequent success has been credited with an increased popularity of fantasy themes and mainstream acceptance of the fantasy
      <a href="/wiki/Fandom" title="Fandom">
       fandom
      </a>
      . "After this weekend",
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN.com" title="CNN.com">
       CNN.com
      </a>
      wrote on the eve of the second season's premiere, "you may be hard pressed to find someone who isn't a fan of some form of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epic_fantasy" title="Epic fantasy">
       epic fantasy
      </a>
      ". According to
      <a href="/wiki/Ian_Bogost" title="Ian Bogost">
       Ian Bogost
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      continues a trend of successful screen adaptations, beginning with
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">
       Peter Jackson
      </a>
      's 2001
      <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">
       <i>
        The Lord of the Rings
       </i>
       film trilogy
      </a>
      and continuing with the
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">
       <i>
        Harry Potter
       </i>
       films
      </a>
      , that have established fantasy as a lucrative mass market genre and serve as "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gateway_drugs" title="Gateway drugs">
       gateway drugs
      </a>
      to fantasy fan culture".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The series' success in overcoming prejudices against fantasy was attributed by writers interviewed by
      <i>
       The Guardian
      </i>
      to a general longing for escapism in popular culture, the series' frequent use of female nudity, and its skill in balancing light-hearted and serious topics  dragons and politics  that allowed it to claim the sort of prestige enjoyed by conventional top-tier drama series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014_132-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_March_22.2C_2014-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The series' popularity greatly boosted
      <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire#Sales" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">
       sales of the
       <i>
        A Song of Ice and Fire
       </i>
       novels
      </a>
      , soon republished as tie-in editions, which remained at the top of bestseller lists for months on end.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">
        The Daily Beast
       </a>
      </i>
      wrote that
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      was a particular favorite of many
      <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">
       sitcom
      </a>
      writers, and consequently the series has been referenced in many other TV series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Together with other fantasy series,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has been deemed responsible for a substantial increase in purchases (and abandonments) of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huskies" title="Huskies">
       huskies
      </a>
      and other wolf-like dogs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has also been the basis of additions to the popular vocabulary. The first season's frequent scenes in which characters explain their motives or background while having sex with prostitutes gave rise to the term "
      <a href="/wiki/Sexposition" title="Sexposition">
       sexposition
      </a>
      " to describe the practice of providing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exposition_(literary_technique)" title="Exposition (literary technique)">
       exposition
      </a>
      against a backdrop of sex and nudity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/World_of_A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="World of A Song of Ice and Fire">
       Dothraki
      </a>
      ", the name of the nomadic horsemen appearing in the series, was listed fourth in a list of words from television most used on the Internet, compiled in September 2012 by
      <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">
       Global Language Monitor
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the second season, the media began using "Game of Thrones" as a figure of speech or as a comparison for situations of intense conflict and deceit, e.g., the court battles about U.S. healthcare legislation,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" title="Syrian civil war">
       Syrian civil war
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or power struggles in the Chinese government.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
