          <td>
           94
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MetacriticS4_144-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-MetacriticS4-144">
             <span>
              [
             </span>
             144
             <span>
              ]
             </span>
            </a>
           </sup>
          </td>
          <td>
           91
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MetacriticS5_145-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-MetacriticS5-145">
             <span>
              [
             </span>
             145
             <span>
              ]
             </span>
            </a>
           </sup>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The critical response to the five aired seasons of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has been very positive. All seasons were listed on several yearly "best of" lists published by U.S. media, such as the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post">
        Washington Post
       </a>
      </i>
      (2011),
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TIME_Magazine" title="TIME Magazine">
        TIME
       </a>
      </i>
      (2011 and 2012) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">
        The Hollywood Reporter
       </a>
      </i>
      (2012).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Seasons 2 through 5 obtained a
      <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">
       Metacritic
      </a>
      rating of 90 or more, which the website rates "universal acclaim". In 2013, the
      <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">
       Writers Guild of America
      </a>
      placed
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      in the fortieth place on the list of the 101 best-written TV series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013WGABestever_149-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-2013WGABestever-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The performances of the very large, predominantly British and Irish cast have been widely praised. American actor
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">
       Peter Dinklage
      </a>
      's "charming, morally ambiguous, and self-aware"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      portrayal of Tyrion, which won him an
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actor_in_a_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actor in a Drama Series">
       Emmy
      </a>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor_%E2%80%93_Series,_Miniseries_or_Television_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actor  Series, Miniseries or Television Film">
       Golden Globe
      </a>
      award, among others, was particularly noted. "In many ways, "Game of Thrones" belongs to Dinklage", wrote Mary McNamara of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">
        L.A. Times
       </a>
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Times_April_15.2C_2011_151-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Times_April_15.2C_2011-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      even before, in season 2, the "
      <a href="/wiki/Scene_stealer" title="Scene stealer">
       scene-stealing
      </a>
      actor's"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salon_March_29.2C_2012_152-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Salon_March_29.2C_2012-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      character became the series' most central figure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salon_March_29.2C_2012_152-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Salon_March_29.2C_2012-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several critics highlighted the performances of the women
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Times_April_15.2C_2011_151-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Times_April_15.2C_2011-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and child actors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      14-year-old
      <a href="/wiki/Maisie_Williams" title="Maisie Williams">
       Maisie Williams
      </a>
      , already noted in the first season for her debut performance as Arya Stark, received particular praise for her work opposite veteran actor
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dance" title="Charles Dance">
       Charles Dance
      </a>
      (Tywin Lannister) in season 2.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Reviewing the first season, critics noted the high production values, the well-realized world and compelling characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Variety
      </i>
      wrote "there may be no show more profitable to its network than 'Game of Thrones' is to HBO. Fully produced by the pay cabler and already a global phenomenon after only one season, the fantasy skein was a gamble that has paid off handsomely."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The second season was also very well received by critics.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">
        Entertainment Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      praised the "vivid, vital, and just plain fun" storytelling,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">
        The Hollywood Reporter
       </a>
      </i>
      said the show made a "strong case for being one of TV's best series", its gravitas making it the only genre show dramatically comparable to shows such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mad_Men" title="Mad Men">
        Mad Men
       </a>
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Breaking_Bad" title="Breaking Bad">
        Breaking Bad
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">
        The New York Times
       </a>
      </i>
      published a mixed review, disapproving of the characters' lack of complexity and their confusing multitude, as well as the meandering plot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_sex_and_violence">
       Use of sex and violence
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Despite its otherwise enthusiastic reception by critics,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has been criticized for the amount of female nudity, violence and sexual violence against women it depicts, and for how it depicts these themes.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">
        The Atlantic
       </a>
      </i>
      called the series' "tendency to ramp up the sex, violence, andespeciallysexual violence" of the source material "the defining weakness" of the adaptation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlantic_160-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Atlantic-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The amount of sex and nudity in the series, especially in scenes that are incidental to the plot, was the focus of much of the criticism aimed at the series in its
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_1)" title="Game of Thrones (season 1)">
       first
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_2)" title="Game of Thrones (season 2)">
       second season
      </a>
      . Actor
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Dillane" title="Stephen Dillane">
       Stephen Dillane
      </a>
      , who portrays Stannis Baratheon, likened the series' frequent explicit scenes to "German porn from the 1970s".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlie_Anders" title="Charlie Anders">
       Charlie Anders
      </a>
      wrote in
      <a href="/wiki/Io9" title="Io9">
       io9
      </a>
      that while the first season was replete with light-hearted "
      <a href="/wiki/Sexposition" title="Sexposition">
       sexposition
      </a>
      ", the second season appeared to focus on distasteful, exploitative and dehumanizing sex with little informational content.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-io9_2_May_2012_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-io9_2_May_2012-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post">
        Washington Post
       </a>
       '
      </i>
      s Anna Holmes, the nude scenes appeared to be aimed mainly at titillating heterosexual men, right down to the Brazilian waxes sported by the women in the series' faux-medieval setting, which made these scenes alienating to other viewers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      And in the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huffington_Post" title="Huffington Post">
        Huffington Post
       </a>
      </i>
      , Maureen Ryan likewise noted that
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      mostly presented women naked, rather than men, and that the excess of "random boobage" undercut any aspirations the series might have to address the oppression of women in a feudal society.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">
        Saturday Night Live
       </a>
      </i>
      parodied this aspect of the adaptation in a sketch portraying the series as retaining a thirteen-year-old boy as a consultant whose main concern was showing as many breasts per scene as possible.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-io9_2_May_2012_162-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-io9_2_May_2012-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_3)" title="Game of Thrones (season 3)">
       third season
      </a>
      , which saw the character
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theon_Greyjoy" title="Theon Greyjoy">
       Theon Greyjoy
      </a>
      tortured at length and eventually
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emasculated" title="Emasculated">
       emasculated
      </a>
      , the series was also criticized for its use of torture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Madeleine Davies wrote in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Jezebel_(website)" title="Jezebel (website)">
        Jezebel
       </a>
      </i>
      that "it's not uncommon that
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      gets accused of being
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torture_porn" title="Torture porn">
       torture porn
      </a>
       senseless,
      <a href="/wiki/Objectification" title="Objectification">
       objectifying
      </a>
      violence combined with senseless, objectifying sexual imagery". But, according to her, the series' violence tended to serve a narrative purpose, except for the titillation and torture of Theon Greyjoy in "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Bear_and_the_Maiden_Fair#In_the_North" title="The Bear and the Maiden Fair">
       The Bear and the Maiden Fair
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A scene in the
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_4)" title="Game of Thrones (season 4)">
       fourth season
      </a>
      's episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Breaker_of_Chains#Rape_scene" title="Breaker of Chains">
       Breaker of Chains
      </a>
      " in which
      <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Lannister" title="Jaime Lannister">
       Jaime Lannister
      </a>
      rapes his sister and former lover
      <a href="/wiki/Cersei_Lannister" title="Cersei Lannister">
       Cersei
      </a>
      triggered a broad public discussion about the series' depiction of sexual violence against women. According to Dave Itzkoff of the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">
        New York Times
       </a>
      </i>
      , the scene caused outrage, in part because of comments by director
      <a href="/wiki/Alex_Graves" title="Alex Graves">
       Alex Graves
      </a>
      that the scene became consensual by the end.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014_168-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To Sonia Saraiya, writing in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">
        The A.V. Club
       </a>
      </i>
      , the series' choice to portray this sexual act and one between Daenerys and Khal Drogo in the first season  both described as consensual in the source novels  as a rape appeared to be an act of "
      <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_fiction" title="Exploitation fiction">
       exploitation
      </a>
      for shock value".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A.V._Club_April_20.2C_2014_169-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-A.V._Club_April_20.2C_2014-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       Times
      </i>
      wrote that critics fear that "rape has become so pervasive in the drama that it is almost background noise: a routine and unshocking occurrence".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014_168-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      George R. R. Martin responded that rape and sexual violence are common in war, and that omitting them from the narrative would have undermined one of his novels' themes: that "the true horrors of human history derive not from orcs and Dark Lords, but from ourselves."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014_168-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times_May_2.2C_2014-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(season_5)" title="Game of Thrones (season 5)">
       fifth season
      </a>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Unbowed,_Unbent,_Unbroken" title="Unbowed, Unbent, Unbroken">
       Unbowed, Unbent, Unbroken
      </a>
      ", Sansa Stark is raped by Ramsay Bolton. Most reviewers, including those from
      <i>
       Vanity Fair
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Salon
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       The Atlantic
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       The Daily Beast
      </i>
      found the scene gratuitous and artistically unnecessary.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlantic_160-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Atlantic-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SalonUnnecessary_170-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SalonUnnecessary-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        170
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_171-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DailyBeast_172-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DailyBeast-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, Joanna Robinson, writing for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">
        Vanity Fair
       </a>
      </i>
      , said that the scene "undercuts all the agency thats been growing in Sansa since the end of last season."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In contrast, Sara Stewart of
      <i>
       The New York Post
      </i>
      wondered why viewers were not similarly upset about the many background and minor characters who'd undergone similar or worse treatment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYPost_174-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYPost-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In response to the scene, pop culture website
      <i>
       The Mary Sue
      </i>
      announced that it would cease coverage of the series because of the repeated use of rape as a plot device,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheMarySueIsSoDone_175-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TheMarySueIsSoDone-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and some viewers, including U.S. senator
      <a href="/wiki/Claire_McCaskill" title="Claire McCaskill">
       Claire McCaskill
      </a>
      , announced that they would stop watching the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DailyMail_176-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DailyMail-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">
        Business Insider
       </a>
      </i>
      cites the negative response to this scene among the possible reasons for the significant drop in ratings between this episode and the next, from 6.2 million viewers to 5.4 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessInsider_177-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BusinessInsider-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fandom">
       Fandom
      </span>
     </h3>

     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Westeros_Wing.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Westeros_Wing.jpg/220px-The_Westeros_Wing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Westeros_Wing.jpg/330px-The_Westeros_Wing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Westeros_Wing.jpg/440px-The_Westeros_Wing.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Westeros_Wing.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        In this
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manipulated_image" title="Manipulated image">
         manipulated image
        </a>
        published by the
        <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
         White House
        </a>
        , U.S. President
        <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
         Barack Obama
        </a>
        , a fan of the series, sits on the Iron Throne in the
        <a href="/wiki/Oval_Office" title="Oval Office">
         Oval Office
        </a>
        with the King's crown in his lap.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire_fandom" title="A Song of Ice and Fire fandom">
       A Song of Ice and Fire fandom
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The novel series
      <i>
       A Song of Ice and Fire
      </i>
      and its TV adaptation
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      have an exceptionally broad and active international
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fan_base" title="Fan base">
       fan base
      </a>
      . In 2012,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">
        Vulture
       </a>
      </i>
      ranked the series' fandom as the most devoted in popular culture, ahead of
      <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">
       Lady Gaga
      </a>
      's,
      <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">
       Justin Bieber
      </a>
      's,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">
        Harry Potter
       </a>
      </i>
      's or
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">
        Star Wars
       </a>
      </i>
      '.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vulture_October_15.2C_2012_178-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Vulture_October_15.2C_2012-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fans include political leaders such as U.S. President
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      British Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">
       David Cameron
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      former Australian Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">
       Julia Gillard
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Dutch Foreign Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Frans_Timmermans" title="Frans Timmermans">
       Frans Timmermans
      </a>
      , who, in a 2013 speech, framed challenges of European politics in terms of quotes from Martin's novels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
       <a href="#cite_note-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2013,
      <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">
       BBC News
      </a>
      wrote that "the passion and the extreme devotion of fans" had brought about a phenomenon unlike anything related to other popular TV series, manifesting itself in a very broad range of
      <a href="/wiki/Fan_labor" title="Fan labor">
       fan labor
      </a>
      , such as
      <a href="/wiki/Fan_fiction" title="Fan fiction">
       fan fiction
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        185
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but also
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      -themed
      <a href="/wiki/Burlesque" title="Burlesque">
       burlesque
      </a>
      routines, or people naming their children after characters from the series:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_March_22.2C_2013_186-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC_March_22.2C_2013-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Arya_Stark" title="Arya Stark">
       Arya
      </a>
      " was the girl's name rising the fastest in popularity in the U.S. in 2012, from 711th to 413th position.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
       <a href="#cite_note-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        187
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Writers cited by the BBC attributed this success to the rich detail, moral ambiguity, sexual explicitness and epic scale of the series and novels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_March_22.2C_2013_186-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC_March_22.2C_2013-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2013, about 58 percent of viewers were male and 42 percent were female, and the average male viewer was 41 years old.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW.com_March_31.2C_2013_188-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW.com_March_31.2C_2013-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        188
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        189
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the marketing director of
      <a href="/wiki/SBS_Broadcasting_Group" title="SBS Broadcasting Group">
       SBS
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      has the highest fan engagement rate of any TV series known to her: 5.5% of the series' 2.9 million
      <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
       Facebook
      </a>
      fans were talking online about the series in 2012, compared to 1.8% of the more than ten million fans of HBO's other fantasy series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/True_Blood" title="True Blood">
        True Blood
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
       <a href="#cite_note-190">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        190
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Among the many
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fan_sites" title="Fan sites">
       fan sites
      </a>
      dedicated to the TV and novel series,
      <i>
       Vulture
      </i>
      noted in particular
      <i>
       Westeros.org
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       WinterIsComing.net
      </i>
      (which provide news reports and discussion forums),
      <i>
       ToweroftheHand.com
      </i>
      (which organizes communal readings of the novels), and
      <i>
       Podcastoficeandfire.com
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vulture_October_15.2C_2012_178-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Vulture_October_15.2C_2012-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are also many
      <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">
       podcasts
      </a>
      covering the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        191
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Viewer_numbers">
       Viewer numbers
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The first season of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      had an average of 2.5 million viewers for its first Sunday night screenings, and an average gross audience of 9.3 million viewers per episode including all repeats and on-demand viewings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
       <a href="#cite_note-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For its second season,
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      had an average gross audience of 11.6 million viewers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        193
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The third season was watched by 14.2 million, making
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      the second most-viewed HBO series after
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">
        The Sopranos
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        194
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
       <a href="#cite_note-195">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        195
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the fourth season, HBO said that its average gross audience of 18.4 million viewers, later adjusted to 18.6 million, had beaten
      <i>
       The Sopranos
      </i>
      for the record.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
       <a href="#cite_note-196">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        196
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
       <a href="#cite_note-197">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        197
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The following graph shows viewer numbers for the first airings:

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">
       Awards
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Game_of_Thrones" title="List of awards and nominations received by Game of Thrones">
       List of awards and nominations received by Game of Thrones
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first season of
      <i>
       Game of Thrones
      </i>
      was nominated for thirteen of the 2011
      <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">
       Emmy Awards
      </a>
      , including
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Drama Series">
       Outstanding Drama Series
      </a>
      . It won two,
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actor_in_a_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actor in a Drama Series">
       Outstanding Supporting Actor in a Drama Series
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Main_Title_Design" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Main Title Design">
       Outstanding Main Title Design
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dinklage" title="Peter Dinklage">
       Peter Dinklage
      </a>
      , who plays Tyrion Lannister, was named Best Supporting Actor by the Emmys, the
      <a href="/wiki/69th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="69th Golden Globe Awards">
       Golden Globes
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/2011_Scream_Awards" title="2011 Scream Awards">
       Scream Awards
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Awards" title="Satellite Awards">
       Satellite Awards
      </a>
      . In 2012, the second season won six of the
      <a href="/wiki/64th_Primetime_Creative_Arts_Emmy_Awards" title="64th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards">
       Creative Arts Emmy Awards
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable" style="width:99%;">

        <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor_%E2%80%93_Series,_Miniseries_or_Television_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actor  Series, Miniseries or Television Film">

        </a>
       </td>
